providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(absAddr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n346: \tif schema == nil {\n347: \t\t// It shouldn't be possible to get this far in any real scenario\n348: \t\t// without a schema, but we might end up here in contrived tests that\n349: \t\t// fail to set up their world properly.\n350: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: no resource type schema available\", absAddr)\n351: \t}\n352: \n353: \tsrc, err := obj.Encode(schema.ImpliedType(), currentVersion)\n354: \tif err != nil {\n355: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode %s in state: %s\", absAddr, err)\n356: \t}\n357: \n358: \twrite(src)\n359: \treturn nil\n360: }\n361: \n362: // planDestroy returns a plain destroy diff.\n363: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDestroy(ctx EvalContext, currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n364: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n365: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n366: \n367: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n368: \n369: \tif n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.Type == \"\" {\n370: \t\tif deposedKey == \"\" {\n371: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"planDestroy for %s does not have ProviderAddr set\", absAddr))\n372: \t\t} else {\n373: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"planDestroy for %s (deposed %s) does not have ProviderAddr set\", absAddr, deposedKey))\n374: \t\t}\n375: \t}\n376: \n377: \t// If there is no state or our attributes object is null then we're already\n378: \t// destroyed.\n379: \tif currentState == nil || currentState.Value.IsNull() {\n380: \t\t// We still need to generate a NoOp change, because that allows\n381: \t\t// outside consumers of the plan to distinguish between us affirming\n382: \t\t// that we checked something and concluded no changes were needed\n383: \t\t// vs. that something being entirely excluded e.g. due to -target.\n384: \t\tnoop := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n385: \t\t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n386: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n387: \t\t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n388: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n389: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.NoOp,\n390: \t\t\t\tBefore: \t\t\tPlannedState: nullVal,\n423: \t\t}\n424: \t} else {\n425: \t\t// Allow the provider to check the destroy plan, and insert any\n426: \t\t// necessary private data.\n427: \t\tresp = have a config for all destroys, but we want to reference\n437: \t\t// it in the diagnostics if we do.\n438: \t\tif n.Config != nil {\n439: \t\t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n440: \t\t}\n441: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n442: \t\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n443: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n444: \t\t}\n445: \n446: \t\t// Check that the provider returned a null value here, since that is the\n447: \t\t// only valid value for a destroy plan.\n448: \t\tif !resp.PlannedState.IsNull() {\n449: \t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n450: \t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n451: \t\t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid plan\",\n452: \t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n453: \t\t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned a non-null destroy value for %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n454: \t\t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr),\n455: \t\t\t),\n456: \t\t\t)\n457: \t\t\treturn plan, diags\n458: \t\t}\n459: \t}\n460: \n461: \t// Plan is always the same for a destroy.\n462: \tplan = &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n463: \t\tAddr:        absAddr,\n464: \t\tPrevRunAddr: n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n465: \t\tDeposedKey:  deposedKey,\n466: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n467: \t\t\tAction: plans.Delete,\n468: \t\t\tBefore: currentState.Value,\n469: \t\t\tAfter:  nullVal,\n470: \t\t},\n471: \t\tPrivate:      resp.PlannedPrivate,\n472: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n473: \t}\n474: \n475: \treturn plan, diags\n476: }\n477: \n478: // planForget returns a Forget change.\n479: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planForget(ctx EvalContext, currentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n480: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n481: \tvar plan *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n482: \n483: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n484: \n485: \t// If there planned change for an instance object into the set of\n526: // global planned changes.\n527: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) writeChange(ctx EvalContext, change *plans.ResourceInstanceChange, deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the set of changes.\n533: \t\tchanges.RemoveResourceInstanceChange(n.Addr, deposedKey)\n534: \t\treturn nil\n535: \t}\n536: \n537: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n538: \tif err != nil {\n539: \t\treturn err\n540: \t}\n541: \n542: \tif change.Addr.String() != n.Addr.String() || change.DeposedKey != deposedKey {\n543: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n544: \t\tpanic(\"inconsistent address and/or deposed key in writeChange\")\n545: \t}\n546: \tif change.PrevRunAddr.Resource.Resource.Type == \"\" {\n547: \t\t// Should never happen, and indicates a bug in the caller.\n548: \t\t// (The change.Encode function actually has its own fixup to just\n549: \t\t// quietly make this match change.Addr in the incorrect case, but we\n550: \t\t// intentionally panic here in order to catch incorrect callers where\n551: \t\t// the stack trace will hopefully be actually useful. The tolerance\n552: \t\t// at the next layer down is mainly to accommodate sloppy input in\n553: \t\t// older tests.)\n554: \t\tpanic(\"unpopulated ResourceInstanceChange.PrevRunAddr in writeChange\")\n555: \t}\n556: \n557: \tri := n.Addr.Resource\n558: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(ri.Resource)\n559: \tif schema == nil {\n560: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n561: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", ri.Resource.Type)\n562: \t}\n563: \n564: \tcsrc, err := change.Encode(schema.ImpliedType())\n565: \tif err != nil {\n566: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed to encode planned changes for %s: %s\", n.Addr, err)\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tchanges.AppendResourceInstanceChange(csrc)\n570: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n571: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s\", change.Action, n.Addr)\n572: \t} else {\n573: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] writeChange: recorded %s change for %s deposed object %s\", change.Action, n.Addr, deposedKey)\n574: \t}\n575: \n576: \treturn nil\n577: }\n578: \n579: // refresh does a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n581: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n582: \tabsAddr := n.Addr\n583: \tif deposedKey == states.NotDeposed {\n584: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s\", absAddr)\n585: \t} else {\n586: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] NodeAbstractResourceInstance.refresh for %s (deposed object %s)\", absAddr, deposedKey)\n587: \t}\n588: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n589: \tif err != nil {\n590: \t\treturn state, diags.Append(err)\n591: \t}\n592: \t// If we have no state, we don't do any refreshing\n593: \tif state == nil {\n594: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] refresh: %s: no state, so not refreshing\", absAddr)\n595: \t\treturn state, diags\n596: \t}\n597: \n598: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.Resource.ContainingResource())\n599: \tif schema == nil {\n600: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n601: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type))\n602: \t\treturn state, diags\n603: \t}\n604: \n605: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n606: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n607: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n608: \t\treturn state, diags\n609: \t}\n610: \n611: \t// Call pre-refresh hook\n612: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n613: \t\treturn h.PreRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, state.Value)\n614: \t}))\n615: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n616: \t\treturn state, diags\n617: \t}\n618: \n619: \t// Refresh!\n620: \tpriorVal := state.Value\n621: \n622: \t// Unmarked before sending to provider\n623: \tvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n624: \tif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n625: \t\tpriorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n626: \t}\n627: \n628: \tvar resp providers.ReadResourceResponse\n629: \tif n.override != nil {\n630: \t\t// If we have an override set for this resource, we don't want to talk\n631: \t\t// to the provider so we'll just return whatever was in state.\n632: \t\tresp = providers.ReadResourceResponse{\n633: \t\t\tNewState: priorVal,\n634: \t\t}\n635: \t} else {\n636: \t\tresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n637: \t\t\tTypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n638: \t\t\tPriorState:   priorVal,\n639: \t\t\tPrivate:      state.Private,\n640: \t\t\tProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n641: \t\t})\n642: \t}\n643: \tif n.Config != nil {\n644: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(n.Config.Config, n.Addr.String())\n645: \t}\n646: \n647: \tdiags = diags.Append(resp.Diagnostics)\n648: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n649: \t\treturn state, diags\n650: \t}\n651: \n652: \tif resp.NewState == cty.NilVal {\n653: \t\t// This ought not to happen in real cases since it's not possible to\n654: \t\t// send NilVal over the plugin RPC channel, but it can come up in\n655: \t\t// tests due to sloppy mocking.\n656: \t\tpanic(\"new state is cty.NilVal\")\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tif !resp.NewState.IsWhollyKnown() {\n660: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n661: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n662: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n663: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n664: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n665: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, \"The returned state contains unknown values\",\n666: \t\t\t),\n667: \t\t))\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \tfor _, err := range resp.NewState.Type().TestConformance(schema.ImpliedType()) {\n671: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n672: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n673: \t\t\t\"Provider produced invalid object\",\n674: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\n675: \t\t\t\t\"Provider %q planned an invalid value for %s during refresh: %s.\\n\\nThis is a bug in the provider, which should be reported in the provider's own issue tracker.\",\n676: \t\t\t\tn.ResolvedProvider.Provider, absAddr, tfdiags.FormatError(err),\n677: \t\t\t),\n678: \t\t))\n679: \t}\n680: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n681: \t\treturn state, diags\n682: \t}\n683: \n684: \tnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n685: \tif !newState.RawEquals(resp.NewState) {\n686: \t\t// We had to fix up this object in some way, and we still need to\n687: \t\t// accept any changes for compatibility, so all we can do is log a\n688: \t\t// warning about the change.\n689: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] Provider %q produced an invalid new value containing null blocks for %q during refresh\\n\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider, n.Addr)\n690: \t}\n691: \n692: \tret := state.DeepCopy()\n693: \tret.Value = newState\n694: \tret.Private = resp.Private\n695: \n696: \t// We have no way to exempt provider using the legacy SDK from this check,\n697: \t// so we can only log inconsistencies with the updated state values.\n698: \t// In most cases these are not errors anyway, and represent \"drift\" from\n699: \t// external changes which will be handled by the subsequent plan.\n700: \tif errs := objchange.AssertObjectCompatible(schema, priorVal, ret.Value); len(errs) > 0 {\n701: \t\tvar buf strings.Builder\n702: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"[WARN] Provider %q produced an unexpected new value for %s during refresh.\", n.ResolvedProvider.Provider.String(), absAddr)\n703: \t\tfor _, err := range errs {\n704: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"\\n      - %s\", tfdiags.FormatError(err))\n705: \t\t}\n706: \t\tlog.Print(buf.String())\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n710: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n711: \t\treturn h.PostRefresh(absAddr, deposedKey, priorVal, ret.Value)\n712: \t}))\n713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n714: \t\treturn ret, diags\n715: \t}\n716: \n717: \t// Mark the value if necessary\n718: \tif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n719: \t\tret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n720: \t}\n721: \n722: \treturn ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \tprovider, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n737: \tif err != nil {\n738: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags.Append(err)\n739: \t}\n740: \n741: \tschema, _ := providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(resource)\n742: \tif schema == nil {\n743: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n744: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider does not support resource type %q\", resource.Type))\n745: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n746: \t}\n747: \n748: \t// If we're importing and generating config, generate it now.\n749: \tif n.Config == nil {\n750: \t\t// This shouldn't happen. A node that isn't generating config should\n751: \t\t// have embedded config, and the rest of Terraform should enforce this.\n752: \t\t// If, however, we didn't do things correctly the next line will panic,\n753: \t\t// so let's not do that and return an error message with more context.\n754: \n755: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n756: \t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n757: \t\t\t\"Resource has no configuration\",\n758: \t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Terraform attempted to process a resource at %s that has no configuration. This is a bug in Terraform; please report it!\", n.Addr.String())))\n759: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n760: \t}\n761: \n762: \tconfig := *n.Config\n763: \n764: \tcheckRuleSeverity := tfdiags.Error\n765: \tif n.preDestroyRefresh {\n766: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity = tfdiags.Warning\n767: \t}\n768: \n769: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n770: \t\t// If we already planned the action, we stick to that plan\n771: \t\tcreateBeforeDestroy = plannedChange.Action == plans.CreateThenDelete\n772: \t}\n773: \n774: \t// Evaluate the configuration\n775: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(n.Config.ForEach, ctx)\n776: \n777: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n778: \n779: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n780: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n781: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n782: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n783: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n784: \t)\n785: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n786: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n787: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed preconditions prevent further evaluation\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \t// If we have a previous plan and the action was a noop, then the only\n791: \t// reason we're in this method was to evaluate the preconditions. There's\n792: \t// no need to re-plan this resource.\n793: \tif plannedChange != nil && plannedChange.Action == plans.NoOp {\n794: \t\treturn plannedChange, currentState.DeepCopy(), keyData, diags\n795: \t}\n796: \n797: \torigConfigVal, _, configDiags := ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n798: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n799: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n800: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n801: \t}\n802: \n803: \tmetaConfigVal, metaDiags := n.providerMetas(ctx)\n804: \tdiags = diags.Append(metaDiags)\n805: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n806: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n807: \t}\n808: \n809: \tvar priorVal cty.Value\n810: \tvar priorValTainted cty.Value\n811: \tvar priorPrivate []byte\n812: \tif currentState != nil {\n813: \t\tif currentState.Status != states.ObjectTainted {\n814: \t\t\tpriorVal = currentState.Value\n815: \t\t\tpriorPrivate = currentState.Private\n816: \t\t} else {\n817: \t\t\t// If the prior state is tainted then we'll proceed below like\n818: \t\t\t// we're creating an entirely new object, but then turn it into\n819: \t\t\t// a synthetic \"Replace\" change at the end, creating the same\n820: \t\t\t// result as if the provider had marked at least one argument\n821: \t\t\t// change as \"requires replacement\".\n822: \t\t\tpriorValTainted = currentState.Value\n823: \t\t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n824: \t\t}\n825: \t} else {\n826: \t\tpriorVal = cty.NullVal(schema.ImpliedType())\n827: \t}\n828: \n829: \tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Re-validating config for %q\", n.Addr)\n830: \t// Allow the provider to validate the final set of values.  The config was\n831: \t// statically validated early on, but there may have been unknown values\n832: \t// which the provider could not validate at the time.\n833: \t//\n834: \t// TODO: It would be more correct to validate the config after\n835: \t// ignore_changes has been applied, but the current implementation cannot\n836: \t// exclude computed-only attributes when given the `all` option.\n837: \n838: \t// we must unmark and use the original config, since the ignore_changes\n839: \t// handling below needs access to the marks.\n840: \tunmarkedConfigVal, _ := origConfigVal.UnmarkDeep()\n841: \tvalidateResp := provider.ValidateResourceConfig(\n842: \t\tproviders.ValidateResourceConfigRequest{\n843: \t\t\tTypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n844: \t\t\tConfig:   unmarkedConfigVal,\n845: \t\t},\n846: \t)\n847: \tdiags = diags.Append(validateResp.Diagnostics.InConfigBody(config.Config, n.Addr.String()))\n848: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n849: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n850: \t}\n851: \n852: \t// ignore_changes is meant to only apply to the configuration, so it must\n853: \t// be applied before we generate a plan. \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n1705: \n1706: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n1707: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n1708: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n1709: preconditions prevent further evaluation\n1715: \t}\n1716: \n1717: \tvar configDiags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1718: \tconfigVal, _, configDiags = ctx.EvaluateBlock(config.Config, schema, nil, keyData)\n1719: \tdiags = diags.Append(configDiags)\n1720: \tif configDiags.HasErrors() {\n1721: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1722: \t}\n1723: \n1724: \tcheck, nested := n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := configVal.IsWhollyKnown()\n1751: \tdepsPending := n.dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx)\n1752: \t// If our configuration contains any unknown values, or we depend on any\n1753: \t// unknown values !configKnown {\n1757: \t\t// We can't plan any changes if we're only refreshing, so the only\n1758: \t\t// value we can set here is whatever was in state previously.\n1759: \t\tif skipPlanChanges {\n1760: \t\t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1761: \t\t\t\tValue:  priorVal,\n1762: \t\t\t\tStatus: states.ObjectReady,\n1763: \t\t\t}\n1764: \n1765: \t\t\treturn nil, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1766: \t\t}\n1767: \n1768: \t\tvar reason plans.ResourceInstanceChangeActionReason\n1769: \t\tswitch {\n1770: \t\tcase !configKnown:\n1771: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: \t\t\t// NOTE: depsPending can be true at the same time as configKnown\n1775: \t\t\t// is false; configKnown takes precedence because it's more\n1776: \t\t\t// specific.\n1777: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] planDataSource: %s configuration is fully known, at least one dependency has changes pending\", n.Addr)\n1778: \t\t\treason = objchange.PlannedDataResourceObject(schema, unmarkedConfigVal)\n1783: \t\tproposedNewVal = proposedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(configMarkPaths)\n1784: \n1785: \t\t// Apply detects that the data source will need to be read by the After\n1786: \t\t// value containing unknowns from PlanDataResourceObject.\n1787: \t\tplannedChange := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1788: \t\t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1789: \t\t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1790: \t\t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1791: \t\t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1792: \t\t\t\tAction: plans.Read,\n1793: \t\t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1794: \t\t\t\tAfter:  proposedNewVal,\n1795: \t\t\t},\n1796: \t\t\tActionReason: reason,\n1797: \t\t}\n1798: \n1799: \t\tplannedNewState := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1800: \t\t\tValue: addrs.NotDeposed, plans.Read, priorVal, proposedNewVal)\n1806: \t\t}))\n1807: \n1808: \t\treturn plannedChange, plannedNewState, keyData, diags\n1809: \t}\n1810: \n1811: \t// We have a complete configuration with no dependencies to wait on, so we\n1812: \t// can read the data source into the state.\n1813: \tnewVal, readDiags := n.readDataSource(ctx, configVal)\n1814: \n1815: \t// Now we've loaded the data, and diags tells us whether we were successful\n1816: \t// or not, we are going to create our plannedChange and our\n1817: \t// proposedNewState.\n1818: \tvar plannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange\n1819: \tvar plannedNewState *states.ResourceInstanceObject\n1820: \n1821: \t// If we are a nested block, then we want to create a plannedChange that\n1822: \t// tells \t// disguise that for a nested block. So,\n1835: \t\t// if we encountered an error we'll tidy up newVal so it makes sense\n1836: \t\t// and handle the error. If so, this resource will be loaded during both plan and apply\n1891: // operations to make sure the check is always giving the latest information.\n1892: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) nestedInCheckBlock() (*configs.Check, bool) {\n1893: \tif n.Config.Container != nil {\n1894: \t\tcheck, ok := n.Config.Container.(*configs.Check)\n1895: \t\treturn check, ok\n1896: \t}\n1897: \treturn nil, false\n1898: }\n1899: \n1900: // dependenciesHavePendingChanges determines whether any managed resource the\n1901: // receiver depends on has a change pending in the plan, in which case we'd\n1902: // need to override the usual behavior of immediately reading from the data\n1903: // source where possible, and instead defer the read until the apply step.\n1904: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dependenciesHavePendingChanges(ctx EvalContext) bool {\n1905: \tnModInst := n.Addr.Module\n1906: \tnMod := nModInst.Module()\n1907: \n1908: \t// Check and see if any depends_on dependencies have\n1909: \t// changes, since they won't show up as changes in the\n1910: \t// configuration.\n1911: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n1912: \n1913: \tdepsToUse := n.dependsOn\n1914: \n1915: \tif n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1916: \t\tif n.Config.HasCustomConditions() {\n1917: \t\t\t// For a data resource with custom conditions we need to look at\n1918: \t\t\t// the full set of resource dependencies -- both direct and\n1919: \t\t\t// indirect -- because an upstream update might be what's needed\n1920: \t\t\t// in order to make a condition pass.\n1921: \t\t\tdepsToUse = n.Dependencies\n1922: \t\t}\n1923: \t}\n1924: \n1925: \tfor _, d := range depsToUse {\n1926: \t\tif d.Resource.Mode == addrs.DataResourceMode {\n1927: \t\t\t// Data sources have no external side effects, so they pose a need\n1928: \t\t\t// to delay this read. If they do have a change planned, it must be\n1929: \t\t\t// because of a dependency on a managed resource, in which case\n1930: \t\t\t// we'll also encounter it in this list of dependencies.\n1931: \t\t\tcontinue\n1932: \t\t}\n1933: \n1934: \t\tfor _, change := range changes.GetChangesForConfigResource(d) {\n1935: \t\t\tchangeModInst := change.Addr.Module\n1936: \t\t\tchangeMod := changeModInst.Module()\n1937: \n1938: \t\t\tif changeMod.Equal(nMod) && !changeModInst.Equal(nModInst) {\n1939: \t\t\t\t// Dependencies are tracked by configuration address, which\n1940: \t\t\t\t// means we may have changes from other instances of parent\n1941: \t\t\t\t// modules. main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx EvalContext, planned *plans.ResourceInstanceChange) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1958: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1959: \tvar keyData evalApplyProvisioners determines if provisioners need to be run, and if so\n2056: // executes the provisioners for a resource and returns an updated error if\n2057: // provisioning fails.\n2058: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: \t}\n2065: \tif when == configs.ProvisionerWhenCreate && !createNew {\n2066: \t\t// If we're not creating a new resource, then don't run provisioners\n2067: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] hook\n2100: \treturn diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n2101: \t\treturn h.PostProvisionInstance(n.Addr, state.Value)\n2102: \t}))\n2103: }\n2104: \n2105: // filterProvisioners []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) == 0 {\n2114: \t\treturn nil\n2115: \t}\n2116: \n2117: \tresult := make([]*configs.Provisioner, 0, len(config.Managed.Provisioners))\n2118: \tfor _, p := range config.Managed.Provisioners {\n2119: \t\tif p.When == when {\n2120: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2121: \t\t}\n2122: \t}\n2123: \n2124: \treturn result\n2125: }\n2126: \n2127: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the resource.\n2133: \tself := state.Value\n2134: \n2135: \tvar evalScope func(EvalContext, hcl.Body, cty.Value, *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n2136: \tswitch when {\n2137: \tcase {\n2152: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] applyProvisioners: provisioning %s with %q\", n.Addr, prov.Type)\n2153: \n2154: \t\t// Get the provisioner\n2155: \t\tprovisioner, err := {\n2162: \t\t\t// This error probably won't be a great diagnostic, but in practice\n2163: \t\t\t// we typically catch this problem long before we get here, so\n2164: \t\t\t// it should be rare to // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package states\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"sort\"\n8: \n9: \t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n10: \tctyjson \"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty/json\"\n11: \n12: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\"\n13: )\n14: \n15: // ResourceInstanceObject is the local representation of a specific remote\n16: // object associated with a resource instance. In practice not all remote\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\n18: // but this is the most common case.\n19: //\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\n23: \t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\n24: \t// Terraform.\n25: \tValue cty.Value\n26: \n27: \t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\n28: \t// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in\n29: \t// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so\n30: \t// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.\n31: \tPrivate []byte\n32: \n33: \t// Status represents the \"readiness\" of the object as of the last time\n34: \t// it was updated.\n35: \tStatus ObjectStatus\n36: \n37: \t// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this\n38: \t// instance dependeded on when it was applied. This is used to construct\n39: \t// the dependency relationships for an object whose configuration is no\n40: \t// longer available, such as if it has been removed from configuration\n41: \t// altogether, or is now deposed.\n42: \tDependencies []addrs.ConfigResource\n43: \n44: \t// CreateBeforeDestroy reflects the status of the lifecycle\n45: \t// create_before_destroy option when this instance was last updated.\n46: \t// Because create_before_destroy also effects the overall ordering of the\n47: \t// destroy operations, we need to record the status to ensure a resource\n48: \t// removed from the config will still be destroyed in the same manner.\n49: \tCreateBeforeDestroy bool\n50: }\n51: \n52: // ObjectStatus represents the status of a RemoteObject.\n53: type ObjectStatus rune\n54: \n55: //go:generate go run golang.org/x/tools/cmd/stringer -type ObjectStatus\n56: \n57: const (\n58: \t// ObjectReady is an object status for an object that is ready to use.\n59: \tObjectReady ObjectStatus = 'R'\n60: \n61: \t// ObjectTainted is an object status representing an object that is in\n62: \t// an unrecoverable bad state due to a partial failure during a create,\n63: \t// update, or delete operation. Since it cannot be moved into the\n64: \t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\n65: \tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\n66: \n67: \t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\n68: \t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\n69: \t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\n70: \t//\n71: \t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\n72: \t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\n73: \t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. A planned\n74: \t// object stored in state will be incomplete if any of its attributes are\n75: \t// not yet known, and the plan must be consulted in order to \"see\" those\n76: \t// unknown values, because the state is not able to represent them.\n77: \tObjectPlanned ObjectStatus = 'P'\n78: )\n79: \n80: // Encode marshals the value within the receiver to produce a\n81: // ResourceInstanceObjectSrc ready to be written to a state file.\n82: //\n83: // The given type must be the implied type of the resource type schema, and\n84: // the given value must conform to it. It is important to pass the schema\n85: // type and not the object's own type so that dynamically-typed attributes\n86: // will be stored correctly. The caller must also provide the version number\n87: // of the schema that the given type was derived from, which will be recorded\n88: // in the source object so it can be used to detect when schema migration is\n89: // required on read.\n90: //\n91: // The returned object may share internal references with the receiver and\n92: // so the caller must not mutate the receiver any further once once this\n93: // method is called.\n94: func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n95: \t// If it contains marks, remove these marks before traversing the\n96: \t// structure with UnknownAsNull, and save the PathValueMarks\n97: \t// so we can save them in state.\n98: \tval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n99: \n100: \t// Our state serialization can't represent unknown values, so we convert\n101: \t// them to nulls here. This is lossy, but nobody should be writing unknown\n102: \t// values here and expecting to get them out again later.\n103: \t//\n104: \t// We get unknown values here while we're building out a \"planned state\"\n105: \t// during the plan phase, but the value stored in the plan takes precedence\n106: \t// for expression evaluation. The apply step should never produce unknown\n107: \t// values, but if it does it's the responsibility of the caller to detect\n108: \t// and raise an error about that.\n109: \tval = cty.UnknownAsNull(val)\n110: \n111: \tsrc, err := ctyjson.Marshal(val, ty)\n112: \tif err != nil {\n113: \t\treturn nil, err\n114: \t}\n115: \n116: \t// Dependencies are collected and merged in an unordered format (using map\n117: \t// keys as a set), then later changed to a slice (in random ordering) to be\n118: \t// stored in state as an array. To avoid pointless thrashing of state in\n119: \t// refresh-only runs, we can either override comparison of dependency lists\n120: \t// (more desirable, but tricky for Reasons) or just sort when encoding.\n121: \t// Encoding of instances can happen concurrently, so we must copy the\n122: \t// dependencies to avoid mutating what may be a shared array of values.\n123: \tdependencies := make([]addrs.ConfigResource, len(o.Dependencies))\n124: \tcopy(dependencies, o.Dependencies)\n125: \n126: \tsort.Slice(dependencies, func(i, j int) bool { return dependencies[i].String() < dependencies[j].String() })\n127: \n128: \treturn &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n129: \t\tSchemaVersion:       schemaVersion,\n130: \t\tAttrsJSON:           src,\n131: \t\tAttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,\n132: \t\tPrivate:             o.Private,\n133: \t\tStatus:              o.Status,\n134: \t\tDependencies:        dependencies,\n135: \t\tCreateBeforeDestroy: o.CreateBeforeDestroy,\n136: \t}, nil\n137: }\n138: \n139: // AsTainted returns a deep copy of the receiver with the status updated to\n140: // ObjectTainted.\n141: func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) AsTainted() *ResourceInstanceObject {\n142: \tif o == nil {\n143: \t\t// A nil object can't be tainted, but we'll allow this anyway to\n144: \t\t// avoid a crash, since we presumably intend to eventually record\n145: \t\t// the object has having been deleted anyway.\n146: \t\treturn nil\n147: \t}\n148: \tret := o.DeepCopy()\n149: \tret.Status = ObjectTainted\n150: \treturn ret\n151: }\n152: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/terraform--9658f9df@01229f4812304880b267c278f4f46f8fe3b3ab12/-/blob/internal/states/instance_object.go"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01695UpritBuMvrMbc2R5zrR","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Aryasch1jKNSHaGGpLw67d","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update changes for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are applied and stored. Values stored in state contain only marks from sensitive variable references, but when those values are retrieved from state for expression evaluation, schema-defined sensitive marks are added back. This mark difference, detected at the plan comparison phase, triggers a spurious `Update` action despite unchanged attribute values.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **multi-layer sensitivity mark gap** spanning state serialization, graph evaluation, and plan comparison:\n\n### Layer 1: State Serialization Drops Schema Marks\n**File**: `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137` (`Encode` method)\n- When a resource value is written to state, the `Encode()` method unmarksthe value and extracts `PathValueMarks`\n- It saves only those extracted marks to `AttrSensitivePaths` (line 131)\n- **Gap**: The saved marks only include paths from sensitive variable references. Provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes have never been marked on the value because providers don't apply marks—that's Terraform's responsibility\n- **Result**: State's `AttrSensitivePaths` is incomplete, missing schema-defined sensitivities\n\n### Layer 2: Asymmetric Mark Application During Evaluation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:718-723` (in `GetResource()` method)\n- When values are read from state for expression evaluation, the `Decode()` method re-applies `AttrSensitivePaths` marks (instance_object_src.go:89-91)\n- **But then** at lines 718-723, schema-defined sensitive marks are **also** applied via `schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)`\n- This happens specifically because `schema.ContainsSensitive()` is true\n- **Result**: Values returned by `GetResource()` for expression evaluation have BOTH variable-reference marks AND schema-defined marks\n\n### Layer 3: Plan Comparison Uses Only Variable Marks\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:725-1251` (in `plan()` method)\n- The plan method reads the prior state value from `currentState.Value` (line 814)\n- This value from state has only variable-reference marks, not schema marks\n- At line 869, this value is unmarked: `unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n- `priorPaths` captures only the marks that were in state\n- The provider's response (`plannedNewVal`) comes without any schema marks\n- At lines 998-1000, the planned value is re-marked with `unmarkedPaths` (which contain only variable-reference marks)\n- At line 1208, a critical check compares marks:\n  ```go\n  if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n      action = plans.Update\n  }\n  ```\n- Even though `unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)` is true (line 1082), the mark comparison detects a difference\n\n### The Asymmetry\n\n| Context | Marks Applied | Missing Schema Marks? |\n|---------|---------------|----------------------|\n| State file (`AttrSensitivePaths`) | Variable references only | ✓ Yes |\n| Evaluator `GetResource()` output | Variable refs + schema marks | ✗ No (complete) |\n| Plan comparison (`plan()` method) | Variable references only | ✓ Yes |\n\nThe evaluator is the **only** place that applies schema marks, and this is compensatory—it patches the incomplete mark information from state. But the plan comparison doesn't have this compensation.\n\n### Refresh Path Compounds the Issue\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-720` (in `refresh()` method)\n- During refresh, the prior value is unmarked before calling the provider (lines 624-625)\n- The provider returns a new state without marks\n- At lines 718-720, the response is re-marked with the same prior marks\n- **Gap**: These prior marks don't include schema-defined marks, so the refreshed value remains incomplete\n- On next plan, the incomplete marks persist\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n1. **State serialization loses schema marks**:\n   - `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137` - `Encode()` saves only extracted marks\n   - `internal/states/instance_object_src.go:77-104` - `Decode()` re-applies stored marks (line 90)\n\n2. **Evaluator applies schema marks**:\n   - `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:718-723` - `schema.ValueMarks()` applied to values from state\n   - `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:689-695` - For planned objects, schema marks also added via `schema.ValueMarks()`\n\n3. **Plan comparison detects mark difference**:\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1082-1083` - Unmarked equality check passes (values identical)\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210` - **Phantom update triggered by mark inequality**:\n     ```go\n     if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n         action = plans.Update\n     }\n     ```\n\n4. **JSON output manifestation**:\n   - `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go` - Reads `sensitive_attributes` from state's `AttrSensitivePaths`\n   - `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go` - Includes resource changes with incomplete sensitivity maps\n   - `internal/states/statefile/version4.go:717-720` - `AttributeSensitivePaths` stored in JSON, missing schema marks\n\n5. **Refresh preserves incomplete marks**:\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-625` - Unmark before provider call\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720` - Re-mark with old marks (schema marks missing)\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/`** (Graph Evaluation)\n   - `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`: `plan()` method performs mark comparison without schema marks\n   - `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`: `refresh()` method loses schema marks during provider round-trip\n   - `evaluate.go`: `GetResource()` method applies schema marks, creating asymmetry\n   - `marks.go`: `marksEqual()` and `filterMarks()` utility functions used in comparison\n\n2. **`internal/states/`** (State Serialization)\n   - `instance_object.go`: `Encode()` saves incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`\n   - `instance_object_src.go`: `Decode()` re-applies stored marks without schema marks\n\n3. **`internal/command/`** (JSON Output)\n   - `jsonstate/state.go`: Outputs `sensitive_attributes` from incomplete state marks\n   - `jsonplan/plan.go`: Includes phantom changes in plan output\n   - `statefile/version4.go`: State file format stores incomplete sensitivity\n\n4. **Provider Interaction Boundary**\n   - Providers return responses without sensitivity marks (correct design)\n   - Terraform must track sensitivities separately via schema and state\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Initial State Creation**: Resource apply writes state via `instance_object.Encode()` which extracts marks from the value. Provider responses have no marks, and schema marks were never applied during provider interaction, so only variable-reference marks are saved.\n\n2. **State Storage**: `AttrSensitivePaths` in state file contains only variable-reference paths, missing schema-defined sensitivities.\n\n3. **Subsequent Refresh**: In `node_resource_abstract_instance.refresh()`, the prior value is unmarked, losing its reference marks. Provider returns response without marks. The original reference marks are re-applied, but schema marks are still missing. Refreshed state persists with incomplete marks.\n\n4. **Planning Phase**: In `node_resource_abstract_instance.plan()`, the prior value from state is obtained without schema marks. The provider's planned response also lacks schema marks. Both are re-marked with the incomplete prior marks. The unmarked values compare as equal (line 1082), but the mark comparison at line 1208 detects a difference.\n\n5. **Phantom Update Detection**: The condition at line 1208 checks if marks have changed despite action being `NoOp`. Due to the mark gap, the check fails and action is changed to `Update`, creating a phantom change.\n\n6. **JSON Output Manifestation**: When `terraform show -json` is executed, the state's incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths` is serialized as `sensitive_attributes` in the JSON output, showing only variable-reference sensitivities, missing schema-defined ones.\n\n7. **Refresh-Only Amplification**: `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes because the same gap exists in the refresh comparison.\n\n8. **Import Amplification**: `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` shows phantom updates because the imported state also goes through the same incomplete mark storage mechanism.\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe root fix requires **applying schema-defined sensitive marks during state storage**, not only during evaluation retrieval:\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n1. **When Encoding to State**: Before unmarking in `instance_object.Encode()`, apply schema-defined sensitive marks using the schema. These should be merged with the extracted variable-reference marks before saving to `AttrSensitivePaths`.\n\n2. **Eliminate Compensatory Workaround**: Once schema marks are stored correctly, the compensatory logic in `evaluate.go` GetResource() that re-applies schema marks becomes redundant and can be cleaned up or verified as correct.\n\n3. **Refresh Consistency**: Ensure `refresh()` preserves all marks (both variable-reference and schema) by passing the schema information to the refresh logic so marks can be properly restored.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Compare `AttrSensitivePaths` in state file for a sensitive attribute before and after the fix\n2. Verify that `terraform show -json` correctly reports all sensitive attributes, including schema-defined ones\n3. Confirm that `terraform plan` after successful apply shows `No changes. Your infrastructure matches the configuration.`\n4. Run `terraform plan -refresh-only` and verify no phantom changes appear\n5. Test `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` to verify no phantom changes\n\n## Impact\n\nThis bug affects any Terraform user with resources that have provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes:\n- VPN tunnels with sensitive cryptographic material\n- Database resources with password attributes marked sensitive in the schema\n- API resources with secret keys defined as sensitive in the schema\n- Any managed resource where the provider schema declares `Sensitive: true` on attributes\n\nThe phantom updates don't cause functional issues (apply is a no-op), but they create false signals in planning and confuse users about infrastructure drift.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":138,"cache_read_input_tokens":95538,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":138},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a69c0d11-31c2-4975-afcb-1bdce61732d4","uuid":"29f15792-0971-4996-ad79-404a12301c7a"}

Values stored in state contain only marks from sensitive variable references, but when those values are retrieved from state for expression evaluation, schema-defined sensitive marks are added back. This mark difference, detected at the plan comparison phase, triggers a spurious `Update` action despite unchanged attribute values.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **multi-layer sensitivity mark gap** spanning state serialization, graph evaluation, and plan comparison:\n\n### Layer 1: State Serialization Drops Schema Marks\n**File**: `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137` (`Encode` method)\n- When a resource value is written to state, the `Encode()` method unmarksthe value and extracts `PathValueMarks`\n- It saves only those extracted marks to `AttrSensitivePaths` (line 131)\n- **Gap**: The saved marks only include paths from sensitive variable references. Provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes have never been marked on the value because providers don't apply marks—that's Terraform's responsibility\n- **Result**: State's `AttrSensitivePaths` is incomplete, missing schema-defined sensitivities\n\n### Layer 2: Asymmetric Mark Application During Evaluation\n**File**: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:718-723` (in `GetResource()` method)\n- When values are read from state for expression evaluation, the `Decode()` method re-applies `AttrSensitivePaths` marks (instance_object_src.go:89-91)\n- **But then** at lines 718-723, schema-defined sensitive marks are **also** applied via `schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)`\n- This happens specifically because `schema.ContainsSensitive()` is true\n- **Result**: Values returned by `GetResource()` for expression evaluation have BOTH variable-reference marks AND schema-defined marks\n\n### Layer 3: Plan Comparison Uses Only Variable Marks\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:725-1251` (in `plan()` method)\n- The plan method reads the prior state value from `currentState.Value` (line 814)\n- This value from state has only variable-reference marks, not schema marks\n- At line 869, this value is unmarked: `unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n- `priorPaths` captures only the marks that were in state\n- The provider's response (`plannedNewVal`) comes without any schema marks\n- At lines 998-1000, the planned value is re-marked with `unmarkedPaths` (which contain only variable-reference marks)\n- At line 1208, a critical check compares marks:\n  ```go\n  if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n      action = plans.Update\n  }\n  ```\n- Even though `unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)` is true (line 1082), the mark comparison detects a difference\n\n### The Asymmetry\n\n| Context | Marks Applied | Missing Schema Marks? |\n|---------|---------------|----------------------|\n| State file (`AttrSensitivePaths`) | Variable references only | ✓ Yes |\n| Evaluator `GetResource()` output | Variable refs + schema marks | ✗ No (complete) |\n| Plan comparison (`plan()` method) | Variable references only | ✓ Yes |\n\nThe evaluator is the **only** place that applies schema marks, and this is compensatory—it patches the incomplete mark information from state. But the plan comparison doesn't have this compensation.\n\n### Refresh Path Compounds the Issue\n**File**: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-720` (in `refresh()` method)\n- During refresh, the prior value is unmarked before calling the provider (lines 624-625)\n- The provider returns a new state without marks\n- At lines 718-720, the response is re-marked with the same prior marks\n- **Gap**: These prior marks don't include schema-defined marks, so the refreshed value remains incomplete\n- On next plan, the incomplete marks persist\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n1. **State serialization loses schema marks**:\n   - `internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137` - `Encode()` saves only extracted marks\n   - `internal/states/instance_object_src.go:77-104` - `Decode()` re-applies stored marks (line 90)\n\n2. **Evaluator applies schema marks**:\n   - `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:718-723` - `schema.ValueMarks()` applied to values from state\n   - `internal/terraform/evaluate.go:689-695` - For planned objects, schema marks also added via `schema.ValueMarks()`\n\n3. **Plan comparison detects mark difference**:\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1082-1083` - Unmarked equality check passes (values identical)\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210` - **Phantom update triggered by mark inequality**:\n     ```go\n     if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n         action = plans.Update\n     }\n     ```\n\n4. **JSON output manifestation**:\n   - `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go` - Reads `sensitive_attributes` from state's `AttrSensitivePaths`\n   - `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go` - Includes resource changes with incomplete sensitivity maps\n   - `internal/states/statefile/version4.go:717-720` - `AttributeSensitivePaths` stored in JSON, missing schema marks\n\n5. **Refresh preserves incomplete marks**:\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-625` - Unmark before provider call\n   - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720` - Re-mark with old marks (schema marks missing)\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/`** (Graph Evaluation)\n   - `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`: `plan()` method performs mark comparison without schema marks\n   - `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`: `refresh()` method loses schema marks during provider round-trip\n   - `evaluate.go`: `GetResource()` method applies schema marks, creating asymmetry\n   - `marks.go`: `marksEqual()` and `filterMarks()` utility functions used in comparison\n\n2. **`internal/states/`** (State Serialization)\n   - `instance_object.go`: `Encode()` saves incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`\n   - `instance_object_src.go`: `Decode()` re-applies stored marks without schema marks\n\n3. **`internal/command/`** (JSON Output)\n   - `jsonstate/state.go`: Outputs `sensitive_attributes` from incomplete state marks\n   - `jsonplan/plan.go`: Includes phantom changes in plan output\n   - `statefile/version4.go`: State file format stores incomplete sensitivity\n\n4. **Provider Interaction Boundary**\n   - Providers return responses without sensitivity marks (correct design)\n   - Terraform must track sensitivities separately via schema and state\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Initial State Creation**: Resource apply writes state via `instance_object.Encode()` which extracts marks from the value. Provider responses have no marks, and schema marks were never applied during provider interaction, so only variable-reference marks are saved.\n\n2. **State Storage**: `AttrSensitivePaths` in state file contains only variable-reference paths, missing schema-defined sensitivities.\n\n3. **Subsequent Refresh**: In `node_resource_abstract_instance.refresh()`, the prior value is unmarked, losing its reference marks. These should be merged with the extracted variable-reference marks before saving to `AttrSensitivePaths`.\n\n2. **Eliminate Compensatory Workaround**: Once schema marks are stored correctly, the compensatory logic in `evaluate.go` GetResource() that re-applies schema marks becomes redundant and can be cleaned up or verified as correct.\n\n3. **Refresh Consistency**: Ensure `refresh()` preserves all marks (both variable-reference and schema) by passing the schema information to the refresh logic so marks can be properly restored.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1.
